وانما يظهر اثر الاكراه :- ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے، جس کی تقریر یہ ہے کہ اکراہ سے اقوال و افعال باطل نہیں ہوتے تو پھرا کراہ کا اثر کہاں ظاہر ہوگا ؟ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اکراہ کا اثر دو باتوں میں ظاہر ہوگا ، (۱) پہلی بات یہ ہے کہ اکراہ اگر کامل ہو تو اس کا اثر نسبت کی تبدیلی میں ظاہر ہوگا یعنی جو فعل مگرہ کی طرف منسوب تھا وہ منکرہ (بالکسر) کی طرف منسوب ہو جائے گا، بشرطیکہ وہ فعل تبدیلی کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہو، اور تبدیلی نسبت کے لئے کوئی مانع نہ ہو، (۲) اور دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ اکراہ اگر قاصر ہو تو رضا کو فوت کرنے میں اس کا اثر ظاہر ہوگا، نہ کہ اختیار کو فوت کرنے میں یعنی اکراہ قاصر سے رضا فوت ہوگی ، اختیار فوت نہ ہوگا، جیسے کسی کو قید و بند ی مار پیٹ کی دھمکی دیکر مجبور کیا گیا، تو رضا فوت ہو جائے گی مگر اختیار باقی رہے گا۔ پھر تفویت رضا پر تفریح کر رہے ہیں کہ اکراہ چونکہ رضا کو فوت کر دیتا ہے، چاہے اکراہ کامل ہو یا قاصر، تو وہ تمام معاملات جو نسخ کا احتمال رکھتے ہیں اور رضا پر موقوف ہوتے ہیں وہ اکراہ سے فاسد ہو جائیں گے جیسے بیع ، اور اجارہ ، یہ عقود فاسد ہوکر ان کا انعقادرضا پر موقوف رہے گا، یعنی اکراہ کے ختم ہونے کے بعد مکرہ نے ان عقود کی اجازت دیدی تو صیح ہو جائیں گے، البتہ وہ معاملات جن میں رضا مندی شرط نہیں ہوتی ہے جیسے طلاق ، عناق تو یہ نافذ ہو جائیں گے جیسے غیر مگرہ سے نافذ ہوتے ہیں۔ مصنف نے فرماتے ہیں کہ تمام اقرار چاہے اکراہ کامل سے ہوں یا قاصر سے، قابل فسخ تصرف کا اقرار ہویا نا قابل فسخ تصرف کا صحیح نہیں ہیں ، جیسے کسی کو قتل یا مار پیٹ کی دھمکی دیکر یہ اقرار کر وایا کہ بول میں نے ماضی میں غلام آزاد کیا ہے، یا بیوی کو طلاق دی ہے یا بیچ کا معاملہ کیا ہے وغیرہ ، تو اس اقرار سے کوئی حکم ثابت نہ ہوگا ، اس لئے کہ اقرار میں سچ اور جھوٹ دونوں احتمال ہیں ، اور جانب صدق کو راحج قرار دینے کے لئے اقرار حیح ہونا اس پر موقوف ہے کہ مخبر بہ یعنی بصورت اقرار جس کی خبر دے رہا ہے وہ واقع میں موجود ہو، اور یہاں مخبر بہ واقع میں موجود نہیں ہے، اس کی دلیل اکراہ ہے، یعنی اکراہ دلیل ہے اس کی کہ اس نے اپنے بچاؤ کے لئے اقرار کیا ہے، مخبر بہ خارج میں موجود نہیں ہے، لہذا سچ کی جانب رائج نہ ہوگی تو اقرار صحیح نہ ہوگا۔
And where the effect of duress appears: it is an answer to an implied question, the exposition of which is that since statements and actions are not invalidated by duress, then where will the effect of duress appear? The answer is that the effect of duress will appear in two matters: (1) The first matter is that if the duress is complete, its effect will appear in the change of attribution, i.e., the action that was attributed to the coerced (mukrah) will become attributed to the coercer (mukrih), provided that the action has the capacity for change, and there is no obstacle to changing the attribution. (2) The second matter is that if the duress is incomplete, its effect will appear in the loss of consent (rida), not in the loss of choice (ikhtiyar). That is, from incomplete duress, consent is lost, choice is not lost, like when someone is compelled by threats of imprisonment or beating, then consent is lost but choice remains. Then they elaborate on the loss of consent: Since duress causes loss of consent, whether complete or incomplete, then all transactions that are susceptible to annulment and depend on consent will become void due to duress, like sale and lease. These contracts are void and their validity depends on consent, i.e., after duress ends, if the coerced person grants permission for these contracts, they become valid. However, those matters in which consent is not a condition, like divorce and emancipation, become effective just as they are effective from a non-coerced person. The author says: All confessions (iqrar), whether from complete duress or incomplete, whether a confession of a voidable disposition or a non-voidable disposition, are not valid. For example, if someone is threatened with death or beating and made to confess: "I freed a slave in the past," or "I divorced my wife," or "I made a sale transaction" etc., then no ruling will be established from this confession, because in a confession there is both the probability of truth and falsehood, and for the side of truth to be preponderant, the confession being valid depends on the reported matter (mukhbar bih) being actually existent. And here the reported matter does not exist in reality, and the evidence for this is duress. That is, duress is evidence that he made the confession to save himself, the reported matter does not exist externally. Hence the side of truth will not be preponderant, so the confession will not be valid.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the effects of duress. It answers the question: if duress does not invalidate statements and actions, where does its effect appear? The author explains two effects: (1) Complete duress (ikrah kamil) changes the attribution of the action from the coerced person to the coercer, provided the action is capable of such change and no obstacle exists. (2) Incomplete duress (ikrah qasir) only removes consent (rida), not choice (ikhtiyar); thus the coerced person still has capacity to act but lacks willing consent. The passage then elaborates on the loss of consent: any contract that is voidable (like sale or lease) and depends on consent becomes void under duress, but its validity is suspended on subsequent ratification after duress ends. Matters that do not require consent, such as talaq (divorce) and itaq (emancipation), take effect immediately even under duress, because they are not conditional on rida. Finally, the author addresses iqrar (confession): any confession made under duress (whether complete or incomplete) is invalid, regardless of whether it concerns a voidable or irrevocable disposition. The reason is that duress creates a strong presumption of falsehood; since the truth of the confession cannot be verified (the reported matter likely does not exist), it lacks the necessary preponderance of truth. This is a Hanafi position emphasizing that iqrar is a form of news (khabar) that must be truthful, and duress undermines its credibility.

Key Terms
نسبت (nisbat): Attribution or ascription of an action to an agent; complete duress shifts it from coerced to coercer.
رضا (riḍā): Consent or satisfaction; removed by both complete and incomplete duress.
اختیار (ikhtiyār): Choice or free will; not removed by incomplete duress.
اقرار (iqrār): Confession or admission; invalid under any duress because truth is not dominant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the effect of incomplete duress (ikrah qasir) on a person's choice (ikhtiyar)?
A) It removes both consent and choice.
B) It removes choice but not consent.
C) It removes consent but not choice.
D) It has no effect on either.

Key Takeaway
Duress does not automatically invalidate actions; its effect depends on the type of duress and the nature of the action, with iqrar being always invalid.

Khula' Under Duress: Talaq Valid, Compensation Waived
Rules on khula' when acceptance of money is under duress: divorce effective but dower not owed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of duress (ikrah) to distinguish between the validity of a contractual act (talaq) and the obligation of consideration (mal) in khula'.

Core Idea
Duress eliminates consent but not choice; talaq requires only choice, but compensation requires consent.

This passage examines a nuanced scenario in khula': when a wife is coerced into accepting the financial consideration. The ruling is that the divorce takes effect, but the wife does not owe the money. The reasoning hinges on a key usul distinction between consent (rida) and choice (ikhtiyar), and how each affects the cause (sabab) and ruling (hukm) of a contract. This lesson unpacks that distinction and its application in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The issue is khula' (divorce initiated by wife in exchange for compensation) when the wife is compelled to accept the financial term. The passage asks: what happens to the talaq and the compensation?
2
Distinguish between cause and ruling
The author separates the 'cause' (sabab) – the contract of khula' – from its 'ruling' (hukm) – the financial obligation. Duress affects each differently.
In Hanafi usul, a contract's existence and its effects are distinct.
3
Apply the effect of duress on consent and choice
Duress eliminates consent (rida) but does not eliminate choice (ikhtiyar). The wife's acceptance verbally is an act of choice, but consent to the financial term is absent.
Ikhtiyar is the capacity to choose; rida is inner satisfaction.
4
Derive the ruling for talaq
Talaq, as a repudiation, does not require the wife's consent – it is effective upon pronouncement. Since choice exists (the wife performed the verbal acceptance), the talaq occurs.
Talaq is a unilateral act of the husband; the wife's role is acceptance, which is valid with ikhtiyar.
5
Derive the ruling for compensation
Financial obligation requires genuine consent (rida). Since duress negates consent, the compensation is not binding, even though the wife's acceptance is technically valid.
This aligns with the Hanafi maxim: 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' – matters depend on intentions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا اتصل الاكراه : اگر خلع میں قبولِ مال کا اکراہ ہو تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی، اور مال واجب نہ ہوگا، جیسے مدخول بہا عورت کو ایک ہزار روپے کے عوض خلع کرنے پر مجبور کیا گیا ، اور عورت نے مجبوراً قبول بھی کر لیا، تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اور مال واجب نہ ہوگا، اس لئے کہ اکراہ خواہ کامل ہو یا قا صر سبب اور حکم دونوں پر رضامندی کو معدوم کر دیتا ہے یعنی مگرہ نہ تو سب یعنی عقد ضلع پر راضی ہے، نہ اس کے حکم یعنی مال قبول کرنے پر راضی ہے، مگر ا کراہ میں اختیار معدوم نہیں ہوتا، تو اختیار موجود ہونے کی وجہ سے عورت کا مال کو قبول کرنا معتبر ہے، اور جب عورت کا قبول
And if duress is attached: If in khula' there is duress regarding acceptance of the money, then the talaq will occur, and the money will not be obligatory. For example, if a woman who has been consummated with is compelled to khula' in exchange for one thousand rupees, and the woman reluctantly accepts, then the talaq will occur and the money will not be obligatory. This is because duress, whether complete or incomplete, eliminates consent (rida) on both the cause (sabab) and the ruling (hukm), i.e., the coerced woman is neither satisfied with the cause (the contract of khula') nor with its ruling (accepting the money). However, choice (ikhtiyar) is not eliminated in duress, so due to the existence of choice, the woman's acceptance of the money is considered valid. And when the woman's acceptance...
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on khula' (divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation) when the wife is coerced into accepting the financial consideration. The author states that the talaq (divorce) takes effect, but the financial obligation (the money) is not owed. The reasoning is that duress, whether complete or incomplete, removes consent (rida) for both the cause (the contract of khula') and its effect (the payment). However, duress does not remove choice (ikhtiyar). Because choice remains, the wife's acceptance of the money is technically valid as an act, but since consent is absent, the payment does not become binding. Thus the talaq is effective (talaq is independent of rida), but the consideration is not due. This is consistent with the Hanafi principle that talaq does not require rida, while financial obligations do. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the conclusion is clear: the wife's acceptance, though valid as a verbal act, lacks the consent necessary to impose a financial liability.

Key Terms
خلع (khul‘): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid to the husband.
قبول مال (qubūl al-māl): Acceptance of the financial consideration in khula'; under duress, it is valid as an act but not binding due to lack of consent.
اکراہ (ikrāh): Duress or coercion; in Hanafi usul, it eliminates consent (rida) but not choice (ikhtiyar).
رضا (riḍā): Consent or satisfaction; required for binding financial obligations but not for the occurrence of talaq.
اختیار (ikhtiyār): Choice or free will; remains present even under duress, making verbal acts valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the financial compensation not become obligatory in khula' under duress?
A) Because the wife did not utter the acceptance.
B) Because duress eliminates both consent and choice.
C) Because duress eliminates consent, which is required for the financial obligation.
D) Because the talaq did not occur.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, duress removes consent but not choice, so the talaq is valid while the financial compensation is not binding.

Metaphorical Use of 'Wa' for Hal in Hanafi Usul
Explaining the rule that wa can be used metaphorically for hal with Quranic and fiqhi examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when the conjunction 'wa' is used metaphorically for a circumstantial clause (hal) and apply this reading to deduce the correct legal ruling in contractual statements.

Core Idea
When 'wa' indicates a circumstance rather than conjunction, the ruling becomes contingent on the condition described.

This lesson unpacks a key Hanafi usul principle: the letter 'wa' (و) can be borrowed from its literal meaning of conjunction to indicate a circumstantial clause (حال). This affects legal rulings in contracts like a master's promise to free a slave upon payment. We'll explore the linguistic basis, Quranic evidence, and fiqhi applications to see how careful textual analysis changes outcomes.

Guided Path
1
State the rule
Identify that the author introduces the rule: wa can be used metaphorically for hal because both share the concept of coexistence (جمع).
This is a usul principle about linguistic interpretation.
2
Recognize the common cause
Understand that hal coexists with its owner (ذوالحال), and wa literally means conjunction (coexistence). This conceptual overlap allows metaphorical extension.
The shared element is jam' (gathering).
3
Analyze the Quranic proof
Examine the verse '…until when they come to it and its gates are opened.' Determine why wa must indicate hal rather than conjunction: open gates before arrival is more honorable.
Context (honor) drives the interpretation.
4
Apply to legal statements
Apply the rule to 'Pay me a thousand and you are free' and 'Descend and you are safe.' Note that the first clause is imperative and the second is declarative, making conjunction (عطف) unseemly. Thus wa is hal, making freedom contingent on payment and safety on descent.
The grammatical mismatch (insha vs. khabar) also supports hal.
5
Address the inversion objection
Understand the objection that hal marks the condition, but here the condition (payment/descent) and conditioned (freedom/safety) appear reversed. The Hanafi response uses qalb (inversion) to rephrase the original intent.
This shows how usul scholars resolve apparent contradictions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَدْ يُسْتَعَارُ الْوَاوِ لِلْحَالِ بِمَعْنَى الْجَمْعِ أَيْضًا لِاَنَّ الْحَالَ تُجَامِعُ ذَا الْحَالِ قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى حَتَّى إِذَا جَاءُوْهَا وَفُتِحَتْ أَبْوَابُهَا أَوْ وَأَبْوَابُهَا مَفْتُوحَةٌ وَقَالُوْا فِي قَوْلِ الرَّجُلِ لِعَبْدِهِ اذْهَبْ إِلَيَّ أَلْفًا وَأَنْتَ حُرٌّ وَلِلْحَرْبِيِّ انْزِلْ وَأَنْتَ آمِنْ إِنَّ الْوَاوَ لِلْحَالِ حَتَّى لَا يَعْتِقَ الْعَبْدُ إِلَّا بِالْأَدَاءِ وَلَا يَأْمَنَ الْحَرْبِيُّ مَا لَمْ يَنْزِلْ۔

ترجمہ: اور کبھی واؤ کو جمع کے معنی کی وجہ سے حال کے لئے بھی مستعار لیا جاتا ہے، اس لئے کہ حال ذوالحال کے ساتھ جمع ہوتا ہے، اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے یہاں تک کہ جب پہنچ جائیں اس پر اور کھولے جائیں اس کے دروازے“ یعنی اس کے دروازے کھلے ہوئے ہوں، اور فقہاء نے کہا مرد کے قول اپنے غلام سے اد الی الفاوانت حر میں، اور حربی سے انزل وانت آمن“ میں کہ واؤ حال کے لئے ہے، حتی کہ غلام آزاد نہ ہوگا مگر ادا سے، اور حربی کو امن نہ ہو گا جب تک کہ وہ نہ اترے۔

تشریح: واؤ کے حقیقی معنی تو جمع کے ہیں، مگر کبھی مجازاً واؤ حال کے لئے بھی استعمال ہوتا ہے، حقیقت اور مجاز میں مشترکہ علت جمعیت کے معنی ہیں، یعنی حال بھی ذوالحال کے ساتھ جمع ہوتا ہے، اور واؤ بھی جمع کے لئے آتا ہے، اس مناسبت سے واؤ مجازاً حال کے لئے استعمال ہوتا ہے جیسے اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا " حتی اذا جاءوها وفتحت ابوابها یعنی مومن جب جنت میں آئیں گے تو جنت کے دروازے کھلے ہوئے ہوں گے، اس آیت میں واؤ حال کے لئے ہے، عطف کے لئے نہیں ہے، اس لئے کہ مومنین کے اکرام کے لئے یہ مناسب ہے کہ دروازے پہلے سے کھلے ہوں، اور یہ اسی وقت ہوسکتا ہے جب واؤ کو حال کے لئے مانا جائے، اور واؤ کو عطف کے لئے مانا جائے تو مومنین کا آنا اور دروازوں کا کھلنا ساتھ ساتھ ہوگا، جو اکرام کے لئے غیر موزوں ہے، اس لئے کہ معزز مہمان کا اکرام یہ ہے کہ دروازہ پہلے سے کھلا رکھا جائے، نہ کہ آنے کے وقت کھولا جائے۔ اسی طرح اگر کسی نے اپنے غلام سے کہا ”اد الی الفاوانت حر“ یا کسی مسلمان نے حربی سے کہا ” انزل وانت آمن“ تو دونوں مثالوں میں واؤ حال کے لئے ہوگا، عطف کے لئے نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ معطوف علیہ جملہ انشائیہ ہے، اور معطوف جملہ خبریہ ہے، جس کی وجہ سے عطف مستحسن نہیں ہے، لہذا حال کے لئے ہوگا، اور حال چونکہ شرط اور ذوالحال کے لئے قید ہوتا ہے، لہذا عتق ایک ہزار ادا کرنے پر موقوف ہوگا، اور امان نزول پر موقوف ہوگا۔ یہاں ایک مشہور اعتراض ہے، کہ پہلی مثال "وانت حر" حال ہے اور دوسری مثال میں " وانت آمن" حال ہے، اور حال شرط ہوتا ہے، لہذا حریت شرط اور ادائے الف مشروط ہوا، اور امان شرط اور نزول مشروط ہوا، تو یہ تو الٹا ہو گیا، کیونکہ حریت شرط نہیں، بلکہ ادائے الف شرط ہے، اور امان شرط نہیں بلکہ نزول شرط ہے، یعنی اترے گا تو امن ہوگا، اور ہزار ادا کرے گا تو آزادی ہوگی۔ اس کے کئی جواب ہیں پہلا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ باب قلب سے ہے، اصل عبارت یوں ہے، "کن خراجًا وأنت مؤدِّي الألف"، اور دوسری مثال "كن آمنا وانت نازل"، اب درست ہو گیا، کہ ادا شرط اور حریت مشروط اور نزول شرط اور امن مشروط ہو گیا، اور بھی جوابات مطولات میں دیکھے جا سکتے ہیں۔
And the letter waw is sometimes borrowed for the circumstantial clause (hal) due to the meaning of conjunction as well, because the circumstantial clause coexists with its owner. Allah Most High said: 'Until when they come to it and its gates are opened' or 'and its gates are open.' And the jurists said regarding a man's statement to his slave: 'Pay me a thousand and you are free,' and to a harbi: 'Descend and you are safe,' that the waw is for the circumstantial clause, so the slave is not freed except upon payment, and the harbi is not safe unless he descends. Translation: And sometimes waw is borrowed for hal due to the meaning of conjunction, because hal coexists with its owner. Allah Most High said: 'Until when they come to it and its gates are opened,' i.e., its gates are open. And the jurists said that in the statement of a man to his slave: 'Pay me a thousand and you are free,' and to a harbi: 'Descend and you are safe,' the waw is for hal, so the slave will not become free except upon payment, and the harbi will not be safe unless he descends. Explanation: The real meaning of waw is conjunction, but sometimes metaphorically waw is used for hal. The common cause between literal and metaphorical is the meaning of coexistence, i.e., hal also coexists with its owner, and waw is also used for conjunction. Through this connection, waw is metaphorically used for hal. For example, Allah Most High said: 'Until when they come to it and its gates are opened,' i.e., when believers come to Paradise, its gates are open. In this verse, waw is for hal, not for conjunction. Because it is appropriate for the honor of the believers that the gates be open beforehand, and this is only possible if waw is taken as hal. If waw is taken as conjunction, then the coming of the believers and the opening of the gates would occur simultaneously, which is unsuitable for honor, because the honor of a respected guest is that the gate is kept open beforehand, not opened at the time of arrival. Similarly, if someone says to his slave: 'Pay me a thousand and you are free,' or a Muslim says to a harbi: 'Descend and you are safe,' in both examples waw is for hal, not for conjunction, because the first clause is imperative and the second is declarative, making conjunction unseemly. Hence it is for hal. And since hal acts as a condition and a restriction for its owner, therefore emancipation is contingent upon paying a thousand, and safety is contingent upon descending. Here there is a well-known objection: In the first example 'and you are free' is hal, and in the second 'and you are safe' is hal, and hal is a condition. Thus freedom became the condition and payment of a thousand the conditioned, and safety became the condition and descent the conditioned, which is reversed because freedom is not the condition, rather payment is the condition, and safety is not the condition, rather descent is the condition; i.e., he will be safe if he descends, and he will be free if he pays a thousand. There are several answers. The first answer is that this is from the chapter of inversion (qalb); the original phrase is: 'Be a payer of tribute and you are a payer of a thousand,' and the second example: 'Be safe and you are descending.' Now it is correct: payment is the condition and freedom is the conditioned, descent is the condition and safety is the conditioned. Other answers can be seen in the detailed works.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary explains the metaphorical use of the conjunction 'wa' (و) for the circumstantial clause (hal). The author begins by stating the rule: the letter 'wa' can be borrowed from its literal meaning of conjunction to indicate a circumstantial clause because both share the concept of coexistence (جمع). The proof (dalil) is the Quranic verse: 'Until when they come to it and its gates are opened' (until when they come to it with its gates opened). The jurists apply this to legal statements: a master's saying to his slave 'Pay me a thousand and you are free' and a Muslim's saying to a harbi (enemy combatant) 'Descend and you are safe' — in both, 'wa' is taken as hal, so freedom is contingent upon payment and safety upon descent. The commentary elaborates that using 'wa' for conjunction would imply simultaneity, which is unbefitting for honoring believers; therefore, it must be hal. The author also addresses a common objection that this reverses condition and conditional, answering with the principle of qalb (inversion), suggesting the intended meaning is 'Be a payer and you are free' etc. This ruling is from the Hanafi school, relying on the literal meaning of Arabic conjunctions.

Key Terms
الواو (al-waw): The Arabic conjunction meaning 'and', used literally for conjunction (عطف) and metaphorically for hal (حال).
الحال (al-hal): A circumstantial clause that describes the state of the subject at the time of action.
القلب (al-qalb): Linguistic inversion to rephrase a statement so that the intended condition and conditional are correctly ordered.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the legal effect of taking 'wa' as hal in the statement 'Descend and you are safe'?
A) The harbi becomes safe immediately upon hearing the statement.
B) The harbi becomes safe only after descending.
C) The safety is conditional on the Muslim's permission.
D) The descent and safety occur simultaneously.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul principle that 'wa' can be metaphorically used for hal changes legal rulings from immediate effect to conditional, based on context and the need to uphold honor and logical consistency.

The Conjunction 'Fa' and Immediate Sequence in Hanafi Usul
Explains the operation of 'fa' on rulings and causes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that 'fa' indicates immediate sequence (تعقيب) when it enters upon a ruling or a permanent cause, and identify when it may also enter upon a non-permanent cause.

Core Idea
'Fa' signals immediate consequence, but its force depends on whether it enters a ruling or a cause—and the cause's permanence.

This lesson examines a key grammatical-legal tool: the conjunction 'fa' (فاء). In Hanafi usul, this letter can indicate that an event follows immediately after another. However, the rule is nuanced: does 'fa' attach to the ruling itself or to the cause of that ruling? The source passage clarifies the default view and then introduces a correction (تنبيه) that broadens its application even to non-permanent causes. Understanding this is essential for correctly deriving rulings from conditional and causal statements in Arabic legal texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the function of 'fa'
Recognize that 'fa' (فاء) is a particle indicating immediate sequence (تعقيب). Its presence implies that the second event occurs right after the first without delay.
Classical Arabic grammar: 'fa' is for الترتيب مع التعقيب.
2
Distinguish between entering upon a ruling vs. a cause
The passage explains that 'fa' typically enters upon a ruling (حكم), not upon a cause (علة). Because the cause precedes the ruling, placing 'fa' on the cause would not convey immediate sequence—the cause already exists.
Default: 'fa' enters the ruling. E.g., 'If you enter, then you are divorced' — 'fa' is on 'you are divorced'.
3
Identify the exception: permanent causes
If the cause is permanent (دائمة)—i.e., it continues to exist after the ruling—then 'fa' can enter upon the cause because the cause still exists at the time of the statement, so immediate sequence is realized.
Example: 'Rejoice, for help has come'—help (cause) remains after the glad tidings.
4
Apply the rule to the slave-freeing example
'Pay me a thousand and you are free'—the freeing (عتق) is a permanent state, so the payment follows immediately upon the utterance. Even though freeing is the cause, its permanence makes the 'fa' valid.
The author says 'it resembles delayed' because the cause appears after the ruling in effect.
5
Recognize the correct madhhab: non-permanent causes also allowed
The note (تنبيه) states that the correct position is that permanence is not a requirement. 'Fa' can enter upon a non-permanent cause, as in 'Do not pray, for the sun has risen'—the rising is momentary, yet 'fa' is used.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فانت طالق تو طلاق واقع ہونے کی شرط یہ ہے کہ عورت پہلے گھر کے بعد دوسرے گھر میں متصل بلا تر اخی داخل ہو، لہذا اگر وہ دونوں گھروں میں داخل نہ ہو، یا صرف ایک گھر میں داخل ہو، یا پہلے دوسرے گھر میں داخل ہوئی پھر پہلے گھر میں ، یا داخل تو ترتیب سے ہوئی یعنی اولا پہلے گھر میں پھر دوسرے گھر میں مگر دوسرے گھر میں تراخی کے ساتھ داخل ہوئی ، تو ان چاروں صورتوں میں طلاق واقع نہ ہوگی، کیونکہ شرط نہیں پائی گئی۔ مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ اصل تو یہی ہے کہ فاء احکام پر داخل ہو، نہ کہ علت پر، کیونکہ علت پہلے ہوتی ہے اور احکام بعد میں ہوتے ہیں، تو جب فاء احکام پر داخل ہوگی تو تعقیب کے معنی متحقق ہو جائینگے ، اور علت پر داخل ہونے سے تعقیب کے معنی متفق نہ ہوں گے کیونکہ علت احکام سے پہلے ہوا کرتی ہے لیکن اگر علت دائمی ہوتو فاءعلت پر بھی داخل ہو جاتی ہے، کیونکہ علت جب دائگی ہے تو اس کا وجود جیسے حکم سے پہلے ہے ایسے ہی حکم کے بعد وہ موجود ہوگی ، تو تعقیب کے معنی محقق ہو جائینگے، الہذا فاء کا علت پر داخل ہونا سیح ہو جائے گا ، جیسے کسی مصیبت میں گرفتار آدمی سے کہا جائے ” ابشر فقداتاک الغوث خوش ہو جا اس لئے کہ تیسرے پاس مدد پہنچ گئی ، تو اس میں غوث بشارت کی علت ہے، اور علت دائمی ہے جو بشارت دینے کے بعد بھی باقی ہے، لہذا فاءکا علت پر داخل ہو نا صحیح ہوگا۔ ولهذا قلنا : - چونکہ فاعلت دائمہ پر داخل ہوتی ہے، اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ اگر کسی نے اپنے غلام سے کہا اد الی الفافانت حر“ تو مجھے ایک ہزار ادا کر، اس لئے کہ تو آزاد ہے، تو غلام فوراً آزاد ہو جائے گا، اس لئے کہ عشق اگر چہ ادائے الف کی علت ہے، اور علت معلول سے پہلے ہوتی ہے لیکن عتق علت دائمہ ہے، جو ادائے الف کے بعد بھی باقی رہتی ہے، تو گویا یہ علت ( عتق ) حکم ( ادائے الف) کے بعد ہوگئی تو تعقیب پائی گئی ،لہذا فا کا داخل کرنا صحیح ہو گیا، اس کو مصنف کہتے ہیں فاشبہ المتراخی کہ یہ علت دائمی ہونے کی وجہ سے حکم سے مؤخر ہونے کے مشابہ ہوگئی۔ تنبیہ: صحیح مذہب یہ ہے کہ علت دائمہ شرط نہیں بلکہ فاءعلت غیر دائمہ پر بھی داخل ہوتی ہے جیسے مصلی سے کہا جاۓ لا تصل فقد طلعت الشمس، اور صائم سے کہا جائے افطر فقد غربت الشمس تو یہاں فاء کا دخول علت پر ہے، اور علت یعنی طلوع و غروب کے لئے دوام نہیں ہے۔ (ایضاح الحسامی)
Then the condition for divorce to occur is that the woman enters the second house immediately after the first house without delay. So if she does not enter both houses, or enters only one house, or enters the second house first and then the first, or enters in order but enters the second house with delay, then in all four cases divorce does not occur because the condition is not fulfilled. The author says that the principle is that 'fa' enters upon rulings, not upon causes, because the cause precedes and rulings follow. When 'fa' enters upon a ruling, the meaning of immediate sequence is realized, and entering upon a cause would not realize immediate sequence because the cause occurs before the ruling. But if the cause is permanent, then 'fa' can enter upon it because its existence is both before and after the ruling, so immediate sequence is realized. Hence entering 'fa' upon a permanent cause is valid, like telling a person in distress 'Rejoice, for help has come to you' — here 'help' is the cause of glad tidings, and it is a permanent cause that remains after giving the news, so entering 'fa' upon the cause is correct. For this reason we say: Because 'fa' enters upon a permanent cause, if someone tells his slave 'Pay me a thousand and you are free', the slave becomes free immediately, because 'freeing' is a permanent cause that remains after payment. So it is as if the cause occurs after the ruling, so immediate sequence is found. The author says 'it resembles delayed' because this permanent cause becomes similar to being postponed after the ruling. A note: The correct madhhab is that a permanent cause is not a condition; rather 'fa' also enters upon a non-permanent cause, like telling a person in prayer 'Do not pray, for the sun has risen', and a fasting person 'Break your fast, for the sun has set'. Here 'fa' enters upon the cause, and the cause (sunrise/sunset) is not permanent. (From Idah al-Husami)
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage discusses the usul rule regarding the Arabic conjunction 'fa' (فَ) which indicates immediate sequence or consequence. The author explains that 'fa' can enter upon either a ruling (حکم) or a cause (علة). The default ruling is that 'fa' enters upon a ruling, meaning the result immediately follows the condition or statement. If it enters upon a cause, immediate sequence would not typically hold because the cause precedes the ruling. However, if the cause is permanent (دائمہ) — meaning it continues to exist after the ruling — then the immediate sequence is valid because the cause is still present. The example given is telling a slave to pay money because he is free; the freedom is a permanent state, so the payment immediately follows the statement. The note (تنبیہ) clarifies that the correct position is that permanence is not necessary; 'fa' can also enter upon non-permanent causes, as in the examples of quoting a cause for prohibition or permission (like 'do not pray because the sun has risen') where the cause is momentary.

Key Terms
فاء (fa): A conjunction indicating immediate sequence (تعقيب) when entering upon a ruling or a permanent cause
علة دائمة (illah da'imah): A cause that persists after the ruling, allowing 'fa' to indicate immediate sequence
تعقيب (ta'qib): Immediate sequence or consequence, the effect of 'fa' when properly placed

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
'Fa' indicates immediate sequence, and the correct Hanafi position allows it to enter upon both permanent and non-permanent causes.

Effect of 'Bal' in Conditional Talaq
Analyzes the conjunction 'bal' in conditional talaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle for the conjunction 'bal' in constructive speech (insha) to determine the number of talaqs that occur in a conditional divorce statement.

Core Idea
In insha, 'bal' cannot cancel the first part; both parts take effect.

The Arabic conjunction 'bal' (بل) typically turns away from the first statement and affirms the second. But what happens in constructive speech like conditional talaq, where the speaker cannot revoke the first part? This lesson explores the Hanafi usul analysis, showing how 'bal' forces a reinterpretation as two separate conditional oaths, leading to a ruling different from ordinary speech.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic function of 'bal' in khabar
In informative speech, 'bal' turns away from the first and affirms the second. For example, 'Zaid came, rather 'Amr' affirms 'Amr's coming and withdraws from Zaid.
If 'la' precedes 'bal', it negates the first.
2
Distinguish between khabar and insha for 'bal'
In constructive speech (insha) like talaq, the speaker cannot revoke an already issued statement. Therefore, 'bal' cannot turn away from the first part.
The act of divorce is instantaneous and irrevocable.
3
Apply the principle to the example
For 'If you enter the house, you are divorced once, no rather twice', the first divorce cannot be cancelled. The second part must be treated as a separate conditional oath.
The statement becomes equivalent to two independent oaths.
4
Contrast with conjunction using 'waw'
With 'waw', the second part depends on the first via intermediary. After one divorce, the woman becomes non-locus, so the second fails. Only one divorce occurs.
This highlights the critical role of the conjunction particle.
5
State the final ruling and usul justification
Upon condition, all three divorces occur. The justification: 'bal' in insha forces a reinterpretation as separate oaths because invalidating the first is impossible.
Demonstrates Hanafi method of deriving rules from linguistic context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
میں داخل ہوگی ، تو تین طلاق واقع ہوں گی ، بر خلاف عطف بالواو کے امام ابو حنیفہ ان کے نزدیک اس لئے کہ جب ، لفظ بل اول کو باطل کرنے کے لئے ہے اور ثانی کو اس کے قائم مقام کرنے کے لئے ہے، تو لفظ بل کا ساتھ بلاواسطہ متصل ہو جائے ، پس یہ کلام یہ دو یمینوں کے ساتھ حلف کے درجہ میں ہوگا ، پس جو اس کے بس میں ہے وہ ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ تشریح:- حروف عطف میں چوتھا حرف بل ہے ، جس کی وضع اس لئے ہوتی ہے کہ وہ اپنے مابعد کو ثابت کرتا ہے، اور اپنے ماقبل سے اعراض کرتا ہے، جیسے " جاء نی زید بل عمرو تو متکلم بل کے ذریعہ اس کے ما بعد یعنی عمر د کے ” آنے کو ثابت کر رہا ہے اور ماقبل یعنی زید کے لئے محبت کو ثابت کرنے سے اعراض کر رہا ہے، تو زید کا آنا نہ آنا دونوں محتمل ہے ، گویا زید مسکوت عنہ کے درجہ میں ہے، لیکن اگر کلمہ لا بڑھا کر کہتا ہے ” جاء نی زید لا بل عمرو " تو زید کے آنے کی نفی ہو جائے گی ، اب یہ مسکوت عنہ کے درجہ میں نہ ہو گا۔ اب جہاں بل کا ماقبل ایسا ہو کہ اس سے اعراض کرنا آدمی کے بس میں ہو، جیسے مثال مذکور میں متکلم نے زید کے آنے سے اعراض کیا، تو وہاں بل ماقبل سے اعراض کے لئے ہوگا، اور جہاں ماقبل سے اعراض ممکن نہ ہو، تو وہاں ماقبل اور مابعد دونوں کے لئے حکم ثابت ہوگا ، ماقبل سے اعراض خبر میں ممکن ہے، جیسے مثال گذری ، اور انشاء میں ممکن نہیں ہے، لہذا انشاء میں بل کے ماقبل اور مابعد دونوں کے لئے حکم ثابت ہوگا۔ اس کی مثال مصنف نے دے رہے ہیں کہ جیسے کسی نے اپنی غیر مدخول بہا بیوی سے کہا " ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق واحدة لا بل ثنيتن “یہ کلام انشاء ہے، یہاں بل کے ماقبل سے یعنی طلاق سے اعراض ممکن نہیں ہے کیونکہ طلاق دینے کے بعد اس سے اعراض کرنا آدمی کے بس میں نہیں ہے، لہذا وجود شرط کے وقت پہلی طلاق بھی واقع ہو جائے گی اور بل کے مابعد کی بھی واقع ہو جائیں گی ، تینوں ایک ساتھ واقع ہوں گی ، اس کے برخلاف اگر حرفِ واؤ سے یہ کلام کیا ہے " ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق واحدة و ثنتين “ تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک صرف ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی ، کیونکہ اس مثال میں معطوف علیہ بلا واسطہ مشرط پر معلق ہے، اور معطوف یعنی ثنتین معطوف علیہ کے واسطے سے شرط پر معلق ہے، اور واسطہ ذی واسطہ سے پہلے ہوتا ہے، لہذا جب شرط پائی جائے گی تو معطوف علیہ یعنی پہلی طلاق جو واسطہ ہے پہلے واقع ہوگی اور معطوف یعنی دوسری دو طلاقیں جو ذی واسطہ ہے، بعد میں واقع ہوں گی ، اس طرح تینوں طلاق واقع ہوں گی، کیونکہ واؤ جمع کے لئے آتا ہے ،لیکن چونکہ پہلی طلاق واقع ہونے کے بعد عورت غیر مدخول بہا ہونے کی وجہ سے باقی طلاق کا محل نہ رہے گی تو باقی لغو ہو جائیں گی۔ لانه لماكان لابطال الاول :- مصنف ہے بل کے ذریعہ عطف کی صورت میں تینوں طلاق واقع ہونے کی دلیل بیان کر رہے ہیں، فرماتے ہیں کہ کلمہ بل چونکہ اول یعنی معطوف علیہ کو باطل کرنے کے لئے آتا ہے، اور ثانی یعنی معطوف کو اس کے قائم مقام کرنے کے لئے آتا ہے، اس لئے کلمہ بل کا تقاضا یہ ہوگا کہ ثانی یعنی معطوف شرط کے ساتھ بلا واسطہ متصل ہو، جیسے اول بلا واسطہ متصل تھا مگر اول باطل ہو گیا ، اور یہ اس کی جگہ آ گیا، لہذا یہ ثانی بلا واسطہ شرط کے ساتھ متصل ہو، لیکن اول یعنی معطوف علیہ کو باطل کرنا اس کے بس میں نہیں ہے، کیونکہ اول لازمی طور پر شرط پر معلق ہو چکا ہے، البتہ ثانی کو الگ سے شرط پر معلق کرنا اس کے بس میں ہے، تاکہ معطوف بلا واسطہ شرط پر معلق ہو جائے ۔۔تو یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے ثانی کے ساتھ بھی شرط مذکور ہے، گویا شوہر نے دو مرتبہ قسم کھائی ہے، اور یوں کہا ہے ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق واحده “ اور ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق ثنتين “ لہذا جب دخول دار پایا جائے گا تو تینوں طلاقیں واقع ہو جائیں گی۔
If she enters the house, three divorces will occur, contrary to conjunction with waw according to Imam Abu Hanifa. This is because when the word 'bal' is for invalidating the first and substituting the second, the requirement of 'bal' is to connect the second directly to the condition without intermediary, but to invalidate the first with the condition, while this is not within his power. And it is within his power to express the second with the condition separately, so that the second becomes directly connected to the condition. Therefore, this speech will be in the position of an oath with two oaths, so what is within his power is established. Explanation: Among the letters of conjunction, the fourth is 'bal', whose function is to affirm what follows it and to turn away from what precedes it. For example, 'Zaid came, rather 'Amr' – the speaker, by means of 'bal', affirms the coming of what follows, i.e., 'Amr, and turns away from affirming what precedes, i.e., Zaid's coming, so Zaid's coming or not coming is probable; it is as if Zaid is in the position of being unmentioned. But if he adds the word 'la' and says 'Zaid came, no rather 'Amr', then Zaid's coming is negated, and now he is not in the position of being unmentioned. Now, where the antecedent of 'bal' is such that turning away from it is within one's power, like in the mentioned example where the speaker turned away from Zaid's coming, then 'bal' is for turning away from the antecedent. And where turning away from the antecedent is not possible, then the ruling applies to both the antecedent and the subsequent. Turning away from the antecedent is possible in news, as in the previous example, but in constructive speech it is not possible. Therefore, in constructive speech, the ruling applies to both the antecedent and the subsequent of 'bal'. The author gives an example: a man said to his unconsummated wife, 'If you enter the house, you are divorced once, no rather twice.' This is constructive speech. Here, turning away from the antecedent, i.e., divorce, is not possible because after issuing a divorce, it is not within one's power to turn away from it. Therefore, upon the occurrence of the condition, the first divorce also takes place and the subsequent of 'bal' also takes place; all three happen together. In contrast, if he used the letter 'waw' and said, 'If you enter the house, you are divorced once and twice,' then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, only one divorce occurs. Because in this example, the first object (معطوف علیہ) is directly suspended on the condition, and the second (معطوف) is suspended on the condition via the first. The intermediary comes before the mediated. So when the condition is found, the first object, which is the intermediary, occurs first, and the second, which is the mediated, occurs later. Thus three divorces would occur because 'waw' denotes conjunction, but since after the first divorce occurs, the woman, being unconsummated, ceases to be a locus for further divorce, the remaining become null. Because when [the author] said 'because it is for invalidating the first' – the author is providing the evidence for three divorces occurring in the case of conjunction with 'bal'. He states that because the word 'bal' comes to invalidate the first (the object of conjunction) and to substitute the second for it, therefore the requirement of 'bal' is that the second should be directly connected to the condition, just as the first was directly connected, but the first is invalidated and this takes its place. So this second must be directly connected to the condition. But invalidating the first is not within his power because the first has necessarily become suspended on the condition. However, it is within his power to separately suspend the second on the condition, so that the object of conjunction becomes directly suspended on the condition. So this becomes as if the condition is also mentioned with the second, as if the husband has sworn twice, saying 'If you enter the house, you are divorced once' and 'If you enter the house, you are divorced twice.' Therefore, when entry into the house occurs, all three divorces take place.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analytical commentary on the effect of the Arabic conjunction particle 'bal' (بل) in conditional talaq (divorce) statements, as part of Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins by stating the ruling: contrary to conjunction with 'waw', when 'bal' is used in a conditional divorce, three divorces occur. He then explains the reasoning: the function of 'bal' is to invalidate the first part and replace it with the second. In an insha (constructive) context, such as talaq, the husband cannot undo an already-issued divorce, so the intended effect of 'bal' cannot be achieved. Therefore, the second part must be treated as a separate conditional oath, resulting in both divorces taking effect. The author elaborates with examples from ordinary speech: in news, 'bal' can cancel the first statement, but in insha it cannot. He contrasts this with 'waw', where due to the intermediary nature, only one divorce occurs because the second divorce depends on the first, and after the first, the wife becomes non-locus for further divorce. The author then reiterates the proof, emphasizing that the husband's inability to cancel the first forces a reinterpretation as two separate oaths. This demonstrates the Hanafi method of deriving fiqh rulings from linguistic principles.

Key Terms
بل (bal): A conjunction particle used for idraab (turning away), affirming the second part and invalidating the first in the context of 'bal'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man says to his unconsummated wife: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced once, no rather twice.' According to the Hanafi view explained in this passage, how many divorces occur when she enters?
A) One divorce
B) Two divorces
C) Three divorces
D) No divorce

Key Takeaway
In constructive speech (insha), the conjunction 'bal' does not cancel the first part; both parts take effect, leading to the sum of both.

The Particle Lākin: Conditions for Correct 'Aṭf After Negation
Usul rule: particle lākin and conditions for correct 'aṭf after negation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two conditions for correct 'aṭf with 'lākin' after negation and apply them to distinguish coherent linking from independent statements.

Core Idea
Lākin corrects a misconception after negation only when speech is coherent and the negated and affirmed subjects differ.

In Hanafi uṣūl al-fiqh, the precise meaning of Arabic particles carries weight for legal interpretation. The particle 'lākin' (but) is used for istidrāk (correcting a misconception) after negation. But not every 'lākin' creates a valid 'aṭf (coordination). This lesson unpacks the two conditions from the classical text Al-Ḥusāmī: coherence of speech (ittisāq al-kalām) and distinct loci of negation and affirmation (ikhtilāf al-maḥall). You will see how these conditions affect legal rulings in contracts like marriage and acknowledgment.

Guided Path
1
State the rule about 'lākin'
Read the passage: 'lākin' is for istidrāk after negation (e.g., 'Zayd did not come, but 'Amr.'). It corrects the misconception that 'Amr also did not come. Note that 'aṭf with 'lākin' requires two conditions.
The rule applies to 'aṭf of a single word on a single word; for sentence 'aṭf, istidrāk can occur after both negation and affirmation.
2
Identify the first condition: coherence of speech (ittisāq al-kalām)
The passage states that 'aṭf is correct only when the speech is coherent (muttasil), meaning what follows 'lākin' is directly connected to the preceding clause as part of the same utterance. If not, it becomes an independent statement (musta'naf).
Coherence means the two parts are logically and grammatically linked, not separate sentences.
3
Identify the second condition: different loci of negation and affirmation
The negation and affirmation must refer to different subjects or objects. They cannot negate and affirm the exact same thing. The passage gives the example of a slave acknowledged to Zayd, who says 'It was never mine but it belongs to another' – here negation (mine) and affirmation (another) are different owners.
If they are the same, the speech is incoherent, and 'aṭf fails.
4
Apply to the marriage example (missing condition)
A fudūlī marries a woman for 100 dirhams, she says 'I do not authorize it, but I authorize it for 150.' Both negation and affirmation are about the same act (authorizing the marriage). Even though the mahr amounts differ, mahr is subsidiary, so the core is the same. Hence the second condition fails; the speech is independent (musta'naf). This nullifies the original contract (naskh) and creates a new offer that requires acceptance.
The student objection that different amounts give different loci is answered: mahr is subsidiary (tabi'), not the essence.
5
Derive the legal ruling
From the usul rule, we infer that in legal texts, if a negation is followed by 'lākin' with an affirmation on the same subject, the statement is not a valid 'aṭf but a new independent clause. This affects interpretation of contracts, wills, etc.
This rule is used in Hanafi fiqh to determine the validity of conditions in marriage and other contracts.

ترجمہ :۔ اور بہر حال لکن تو وہ استدراک کے لئے ہے نفی کے بعد تو کہتا ہے " ما جاء في زيد لكن عمر ا نگری کہ لکن کے ذریعہ عطف درست ہوتا ہے کلام کے متسق ہونے کے وقت ، پس جب کلام متسق ہوگا جیسے وہ شخص جس کے لئے غلام کا اقرار کیا گیا ہو، (کہے ) یہ میرا ہر گز نہیں ہے لیکن دوسرے فلاں کا ہے، تو نفی اثبات کے ساتھ متعلق ہوگی حتی کہ ثانی اس غلام کا مستحق ہوگا، ورنہ تو وہ کلام مستأنف ہوگا، جیسے وہ عورت جس کا سودینار میں نکاح کیا گیا ہو کہے کہ ”میں نکاح کی اجازت نہیں دیتی لیکن اجازت دیتی ہوں ڈیڑھ سو میں تو عقد فسخ ہو جائے گا، اس لئے کہ یہ فعل کی نفی ہے اور بعینہ اس کا اثبات ہے، پس کلام متسق نہیں ہے۔ تشریح:- حروف عطف میں سے پانچواں حرف لکن ہے، جو نفی کے بعد استدراک کے لئے آتا ہے، یعنی کلام سابق سے جو وہم پیدا ہوتا ہے اس وہم کو دور کرنے کے لئے آتا ہے، جیسے آپ نے کہا ” ما جاء نی زید زید نہیں آیا ، تو اس سے وہم پیدا ہوا کہ عمرو بھی نہیں آیا ہوگا، کیونکہ ان دونوں میں گہری دوستی اور لگاؤ ہے، تو آپ نے ” لكن

عمرو “ کہہ کر اس کی تلافی کر دی ، وہم کو دور کر دیا لیکن اگر مخففہ ہو تو عاطفہ ہوگا، اور استدراک کے لئے ہوگا اور مشددہ ہے تو مشبہ بالفعل ہوگا ، جو استدراک میں عاطفہ کا شریک ہے۔
مصنف اللہ نے نفی کے بعد استدراک کے لئے کہا، تو یہ اس صورت میں ہے جب کہ عطف مفرد علی المفرد ہو
جیسے اوپر مثال گذری، اور اگر جملہ کا عطف جملہ پر ہو تو فی اور اثبات دونوں میں استدراک ہوسکتا ہے۔ غيران العطف به : لکن کے ذریعہ عطف کی صورت میں لکن کے نفی کے بعد استدراک کے لئے ہونے کی دوشرطیں ہیں، (۱) جس کلام میں لکن واقع ہو وہ کلام متصل ہو یعنی لکن کا مابعد ماقبل سے ملا ہوا ہو (۲) نفی اور
اثبات دونوں کا محل الگ الگ ہو، یعنی بعینہ ایک ہی چیز کی نفی اور اثبات نہ ہورہا ہے، تا کہ دونوں جمع ہوسکیں۔ جیسے کسی کے پاس غلام ہے اور یہ اقرار کرتا ہے کہ یہ غلام زید کا ہے، تو زید مقرلہ کہتا ہے ما كان لي قط لكن لفلان آخر کہ یہ غلام میرا نہیں ہے، لیکن وہ فلاں کا ہے، تو یہ غلام فلاں کا ہوگا، نہ کہ مقولہ کا، کیونکہ یہاں دونوں شرطیں موجود ہیں، کہ لکن نفی کے بعد ہے، اور لکن کا ما بعد اس کے ماقبل سے ملا ہوا بھی ہے، اور نفی واثبات کا محل بھی الگ الگ ہے، کہ نفی تو متکلم کی طرف راجع ہے، اور اثبات فلان آخر کی طرف راجع ہے ،لہذا عطف درست ہوگا ، پس غلام کا مستحق فلان آخر ہوگا نہ متکلم یعنی مقرلہ۔ اور شرط مفقود ہونے کی مثال مصنف اللہ نے بیان کی کہ اگر فضولی نے کسی عورت کا نکاح سو درھم میں کر دیا عورت کو جب خبر پہنچی تو اس نے کہا ”لا اجیزہ“ میں اس نکاح کو جائز نہیں کرتی ولكن اجيزه بمائة وخمسين “ لیکن ڈیڑھ سو درھم میں جائز کرتی ہوں تو عورت کے اس قول سے عقدِ نکاح فسخ ہو جائے گا، کیونکہ عورت نے جس فعل کی نفی کی ہے اس فعل کا اثبات کیا ہے، یعنی نکاح کی نفی کی ہے اور نکاح ہی کا اثبات کیا ہے، تو دوسری شرط نہ پائے جانے کی وجہ سے کلام مستأنف اور مستقل ہوگا، اور جب مستقل کلام ہوا تو یہ عورت کی طرف سے ایجاب ہوگا ، اور ایجاب بغیر قبول کے معتبر نہیں ہے، لہذا نکاح منعقد نہ ہوگا، اور فضولی کا کیا ہوا نکاح لا اجیزہ سے نسخ ہو گیا۔ طالب علمانہ سوال: ہوتا ہے کہ عورت کے کلام میں نفی اور اثبات ایک ہی سے متعلق نہیں ہے بلکہ نفی سو درہم کے ساتھ مقید ہے اور اثبات ڈیڑھ سو درھم کے ساتھ مقید ہے، تو نفی اور اثبات کا محل الگ الگ ہو گیا، لہذا اتساق پا یا گیا تو عطف درست ہونا چاہیے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ سو اور سو ڈیڑھ سو مہر ہے، اور مہر نکاح میں تابع ہوتا ہے، اس کا اعتبار نہیں ہے، اسی لئے اگر نکاح میں مہر کا ذکر نہ ہو، یا اس کی نفی ہو تو بھی نکاح ہو جاتا ہے، لہذا عورت کے کلام میں نکاح ہی کی نفی اور اثبات ہے ،تو اتساق کی شرط مفقود ہے، لہذا عطف درست نہ ہوگا۔۔ ہاں اگر عورت اس طرح کہے "لا اجيزه بمائة ولكن
The Fadl al-Hijazi [book]. Commentary in Urdu on al-Muntakhab al-Husami. Because when it is for invalidating the first: the author is stating the proof for the occurrence of three divorces in the case of 'atf with 'bal'. He says: since the word 'bal' comes to invalidate the first (ma'tuf 'alayh) and to substitute the second (ma'tuf) in its place, therefore the requirement of 'bal' is that the second be connected directly to the condition, just as the first was directly connected, but the first becomes invalid and the second takes its place. Hence this second is directly connected to the condition, but invalidating the first is not within its power, because the first has necessarily been suspended upon the condition. However, it is within its power to suspend the second separately upon the condition, so that the ma'tuf becomes directly suspended upon the condition. So this becomes as if the condition is also mentioned with the second, meaning the husband has sworn two oaths, saying 'if you enter the house, you are divorced once' and 'if you enter the house, you are divorced twice'. Therefore when entry into the house occurs, all three divorces take place. 'And as for 'lakin', it is for istidrak after negation. He says: 'Zayd did not come to me, but 'Amr'. However, 'atf with it is only correct when the speech is coherent. So when the speech is coherent, like the one for whom a slave is acknowledged (saying) 'It was never mine, but it belongs to another slave', the negation becomes connected to the affirmation such that the second deserves him. Otherwise it is a new independent statement, like a woman married for one hundred (dirhams) saying 'I do not authorize it, but I authorize it for one hundred and fifty', then the contract becomes void because she negated the act and affirmed the very same act, so the speech is not coherent.' Translation: As for 'lakin', it is for istidrak after negation. He says 'Zayd did not come but 'Amr', meaning that 'atf with 'lakin' is correct only when the speech is coherent. So when the speech is coherent, like the person for whom a slave is acknowledged (he says) 'It is never mine but it is for such and such other', then the negation is attached to the affirmation such that the second deserves that slave. Otherwise it is a new independent statement, like a woman whose marriage was contracted for one hundred (dirhams), she says 'I do not authorize the marriage, but I authorize it for one hundred and fifty', then the contract becomes void because she negated an act and affirmed the same act, so the speech is not coherent. Explanation: Among the particles of 'atf, the fifth is 'lakin', which comes for istidrak after negation, i.e., to remove the misconception that arose from the previous speech. For example, you said 'Zayd did not come', this creates the misconception that 'Amr also did not come, due to their close friendship. So you said 'but 'Amr' to remedy this, removing the misconception. But if it is lightened (mukhaffafa), it is an 'atifa and for istidrak; if it is emphasized (mushaddada), it is like a verb (mushabbah bil fi'l) which shares in istidrak with the 'atifa. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said 'after negation for istidrak', this is in the case of 'atf of a single word upon a single word as in the above example. But if it is 'atf of a sentence upon a sentence, istidrak can be in both negation and affirmation. 'Ghayr anna al-'atfa bihi': In the case of 'atf with 'lakin', for 'lakin' to be for istidrak after negation, there are two conditions: (1) The sentence in which 'lakin' occurs must be connected (muttasil), i.e., what follows 'lakin' must be joined to what precedes it; (2) The locus of negation and affirmation must be different, i.e., they are not negating and affirming the very same thing, so that both can be combined. For example: someone has a slave and acknowledges that this slave belongs to Zayd. Zayd the addressee says: 'It was never mine, but it belongs to another person', then the slave will belong to that other person, not to the addressee, because here both conditions exist: 'lakin' is after negation, what follows 'lakin' is connected to what precedes it, and the loci of negation and affirmation are separate – negation refers back to the speaker, affirmation refers to the other person. So 'atf is correct, hence the slave belongs to that other person, not to the speaker (the addressee). And the example of a missing condition is given by the author: if a fuduli (unauthorized agent) marries a woman for one hundred dirhams, when the woman learns of it, she says, 'I do not authorize it, but I authorize it for one hundred and fifty,' then the marriage contract becomes void because the woman has negated an act and affirmed the same act, i.e., she negated the marriage and affirmed the very marriage. Hence the second condition is not met, so the speech is a new independent statement (musta'naf). When it becomes an independent statement, this constitutes an offer (ijab) from the woman, and an offer without acceptance is not valid, so the marriage does not take place, and the marriage done by the fuduli becomes void (naskh) due to her 'la ujizuhu'. Student question: The woman's speech negates and affirms not one thing; rather, negation is restricted to one hundred dirhams and affirmation to one hundred and fifty dirhams, so the loci of negation and affirmation are different, and coherence is achieved, so 'atf should be correct. The answer: One hundred and one hundred and fifty are mahr, and mahr in marriage is subsidiary, it has no weight. Therefore, if mahr is not mentioned in marriage, or is negated, marriage still takes place. So in the woman's speech, negation and affirmation are about the marriage itself, thus the condition of coherence is missing, so 'atf is not correct. Commentary
This passage from Al-Faiz-ul-Hijaz, an Urdu commentary on Al-Husami, deals with the Arabic particle 'lākin' and its function in 'aṭf (coordination) after negation. The author first briefly reviews the particle 'bal' to contrast it, then focuses on 'lākin'. He explains that 'lākin' is used for 'istidrāk' — correcting a misconception that arises from a negative statement. For example, 'Zayd did not come, but 'Amr.' Without 'lākin', one might wrongly assume 'Amr also did not come. The author then specifies two conditions for correct 'aṭf with 'lākin' after negation: (1) the speech must be coherent (muttasil), meaning what follows 'lākin' is directly connected to the preceding part as part of the same utterance; (2) the subject of the negation and the subject of the affirmation must be different (different loci) — they cannot be about the exact same thing. He illustrates with two examples. Example one (fulfilling conditions): A person acknowledges a slave belonging to Zayd. Zayd responds: 'The slave was never mine, but he belongs to someone else.' Here the negation ('mine') and affirmation ('someone else') refer to different owners, so the speech is coherent and the correct ruling is that the slave belongs to the other person, not Zayd. Example two (missing condition): A woman whose marriage was contracted by a fudūlī for 100 dirhams says: 'I do not authorize the marriage, but I authorize it for 150 dirhams.' Here the negation and affirmation both refer to the very same action (authorizing the marriage), even though the amounts differ. Since the mahr (dowry) is a subsidiary element that does not change the core act, the loci are not genuinely different. Consequently, the speech lacks coherence and becomes an independent statement (musta'naf). This independent statement is considered a new marriage offer (ījāb) from the woman, which requires acceptance to be valid. Since there is no acceptance, no marriage takes place, and the original contract by the fudūlī is void. The author then addresses a potential student objection: the amounts differ (100 vs 150), so aren't the loci different? He refutes this by explaining that the mahr is subordinate to the marriage; the negation and affirmation both concern the marriage itself, not the mahr. Thus the second condition fails. This nuanced linguistic analysis directly impacts legal rulings in marriage and other contracts, showing how precise understanding of Arabic particles is essential for correct fiqh deductions.

Key Terms
لکن (lākin): A particle of 'aṭf (coordination) used for istidrāk after negation, to correct a misconception.
استدراك (istidrāk): Correcting a mistaken assumption (wahm) that arises from a previous statement, often after negation.
عطف (ʿaṭf): Grammatical coordination linking two parts of speech with a coordinating conjunction.
اتساق الكلام (ittisāq al-kalām): Coherence of speech; the connectedness between the clauses so that the 'aṭf is valid.
مستأنف (musta'naf): A new independent statement not grammatically linked to the previous clause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the two conditions for correct 'aṭf with 'lākin' after negation?
A) The speech must be coherent (muttasil) and the loci of negation and affirmation must be different.
B) The speech must be in Arabic and the negation must be clear.
C) The negation must be explicit and 'lākin' must be emphasized (mushaddada).
D) The affirmation must follow immediately and the speaker must intend istidrāk.

Key Takeaway
For 'lākin' to create a valid 'aṭf after negation, the speech must be coherent and the subjects of negation and affirmation must be different; otherwise, the statement is independent and carries different legal consequences.

The Legal Meanings of 'Hatta' in Oaths
Hanafi analysis of 'hatta' as ghayah, sababiyya, or fa-like

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the three Hanafi usul interpretations of 'hatta' in oaths—ghayah, sababiyya, and sequence—to determine whether an oath is broken.

Core Idea
'Hatta' can mean end, cause, or sequence—context decides the ruling.

The particle 'hatta' holds multiple legal meanings in Hanafi usul, especially in oath formulations. Its interpretation depends on whether the second act can serve as a natural end, a cause, or must follow immediately. This lesson draws on Imam Muhammad's rulings in al-Ziyadat to show how to navigate these meanings and derive correct legal outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Classify the relation between the two actions
Examine the two acts in the oath: the first (e.g., beating, coming) and the second (e.g., screaming, feeding). Determine if the second act can be a natural end to the first, a cause, or if both acts are by the same swearer.
Beating can be extended; screaming can end it. Feeding encourages coming.
2
Apply the literal meaning of 'hatta' as ghayah
If the second act can serve as a natural end to the first, 'hatta' retains its literal meaning of ghayah. The oath is fulfilled only if the first act continues until the second occurs.
E.g., 'until you scream': swearer must beat until screaming to avoid breaking oath.
3
Apply the metaphorical meaning of 'hatta' as sababiyya
If the second act cannot be an end but is a cause or favor that motivates the first, 'hatta' is interpreted as 'lam al-sababiyya' (for causation). The oath is fulfilled if the swearer performs the first act with the intention of attaining the second.
E.g., 'until you feed me': coming with intention of being fed fulfills oath even if feeding does not occur.
4
Apply the meaning of 'hatta' as sequence (atf)
If both acts are performed by the same swearer, 'hatta' cannot indicate ghayah or sababiyya. It is then interpreted as 'atf bi al-fa' (sequence), requiring both acts in immediate succession.
E.g., 'until I eat at your place': swearer must come and immediately eat to avoid breaking oath.

بحرف الفاء کے لئے ہوگا، غایت کے لئے تو اس لئے نہیں ہوگا کہ کھانا کھلانا اتیان کے لئے غایت نہیں بن سکتا ہے، اور لام گئی کے معنی میں اس لئے نہیں ہوگا کہ اتیان اور تغد یہ دونوں ایک ہی شخص کے فعل ہیں ، عادہ ایک شخص کا فعل خود اس کے فعل کے لئے سبب اور جزا نہیں بن سکتا، لہذا کھانا کھلانا اتیان کا سبب نہ ہوگا، تو حتی لام گئی کے معنی میں سبیت و مجازات کے لئے نہ ہوگا، بلکہ عطف بحرف الفاء کے لئے ہوگا، اور عطف کے لئے لینے میں مناسبت یہ ہے کہ حتی غایت کے لئے آتا ہے، اور غایت مغیا سے وجود مؤخر ہوتی ہے، اور حرف عطف فا تعقیب کے لئے آتا ہے، یعنی فا کا مابعد اس کے ماقبل سے وجود میں مؤخر ہوتا ہے، تو غایت اور تعقیب کے معنی قریب قریب ہیں۔ اب مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ اگر میں تیرے پاس نہ آیا پھر تیرے پاس کھانا نہ کھایا،تو میرا غلام آزاد ہے،تو آنا اور فوراً کھانا کھانا یہ دونوں قسم پورا ہونے کے لئے ضروری ہیں، چنانچہ حالف مخاطب کے پاس آیا پھر متصلاً کھانا بھی کھایا ، تو قسم پوری ہو جائے گی ، اور غلام آزاد نہ ہوگا، اور اگر حالف آیا ہی نہیں، یا آیا مگر کھانا نہیں کھا یا ، یا کچھ تاخیر سے کھانا کھایا ، تو ان تمام صورتوں میں حانث ہو جائے گا اور غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔
Translation: And in any case, 'hatta' is for ghayah (end). For this reason, Imam Muhammad said in al-Ziyadat regarding the person who said: 'His slave is free if I do not beat you until you scream' that he will be a hanith (breaker of oath) if he stopped before the ghayah. And 'hatta' is borrowed metaphorically in the meaning of 'lam' for sababiyya, as in the speaker's statement: 'If I do not come to you tomorrow until you feed me breakfast' – so when the speaker came to him and the addressee did not feed him breakfast, he is not a hanith because a favor does not have the capacity to prevent coming; rather the favor is a cause for coming. So if both acts are from the same person, like the speaker's statement: 'If I do not come to you until I eat breakfast at your place', then the fulfillment of the oath is connected to both, because one person's act cannot be a reward for his own act. So it is interpreted as 'atf' with the letter 'fa', because ghayah is from the genus of ta'qib (sequence). Sharih: Among the letters of 'atf', the seventh is 'hatta' which comes for ghayah, i.e., what comes after 'hatta' is the ghayah of what precedes it. But 'hatta' is for ghayah when the preceding speech has extension and what follows has the capacity to be an end. For this reason, because 'hatta' is placed for ghayah, Imam Muhammad said in al-Ziyadat that if someone said: 'My slave is free if I do not beat you until you scream', here 'hatta' is for ghayah because the preceding speech has extension – beating can be extended, and what follows, i.e., screaming, can be an end, because a person may stop beating out of mercy upon screaming. Therefore, if the swearer did not beat at all, or beat but stopped before screaming, in both cases he becomes a hanith and his slave is free. If he beat until screaming, he is not a hanith. And if 'hatta' does not have the capacity for the meaning of ghayah, it is taken metaphorically in the meaning of 'lam' for sababiyya and causality, like: 'If I do not come to you tomorrow so that you feed me breakfast, my slave is free'. Here 'hatta' is in the meaning of 'lam' for sababiyya, because it does not have the capacity for the meaning of ghayah, since feeding breakfast cannot be a ghayah for coming; rather feeding is a favor which is a stronger motivator for coming. So 'hatta' will be in the meaning of 'lam'. Now the meaning will be: If I do not come to you for breakfast, my slave is free. The swearer's coming for breakfast is a condition for the slave's freedom. So if the swearer did not come at all, he becomes a hanith. If he came but the addressee did not feed him, he is not a hanith, because the swearer came for breakfast, but breakfast is an act of the addressee over which the swearer has no control. Therefore it will be considered that the swearer came for breakfast, so the oath is fulfilled, he is not a hanith. But if both acts are from the swearer, like: 'If I do not come to you until I eat breakfast at your place, my slave is free', then the oath is connected to both coming and eating. In this case, 'hatta' is neither for ghayah nor for sababiyya in the meaning of 'lam'; rather 'hatta' is for 'atf' with the letter 'fa'. It is not for ghayah because eating cannot be a ghayah for coming, and not for sababiyya because both coming and eating are acts of one person, and a person's act cannot be a cause or reward for his own act. So 'hatta' is for 'atf' with the letter 'fa'. The suitability for taking it for 'atf' is that 'hatta' comes for ghayah, and ghayah is later in existence than what it bounds, and the letter 'fa' comes for ta'qib (sequence), i.e., what comes after 'fa' is later in existence than what precedes it. Thus the meanings of ghayah and ta'qib are close. Now the meaning will be: If I do not come to you and then I do not eat food at your place, my slave is free. So coming and immediately eating are both necessary for fulfilling the oath. Therefore, if the swearer came and immediately ate, the oath is fulfilled and the slave is not free. If he did not come at all, or came but did not eat, or ate after a delay, in all these cases he becomes a hanith and the slave is free.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage is an extensive Hanafi usul analysis of the particle 'hatta' in the context of legal oaths. It begins by stating that 'hatta' can indicate ghayah (end/goal). The authority for this is Imam Muhammad's ruling in al-Ziyadat. The first scenario: If one swears 'if I do not beat you until you scream', the beating has extension and screaming can serve as an end (the swearer may stop out of mercy). Hence 'hatta' is literal here. If the swearer stops before the ghayah (screaming), he breaks the oath. If he beats until screaming, he does not break it. The second scenario: If the second act cannot be an end (like feeding breakfast for coming, since feeding is a favor that encourages coming), 'hatta' is used metaphorically to mean 'lam' for sababiyya (causation). Then the oath is conditional upon the swearer coming for that purpose; if he comes, the oath is fulfilled even if the other does not feed him. The third scenario: If both acts are by the same person (e.g., 'if I do not come and eat at your place'), 'hatta' cannot indicate ghayah or causation, so it is interpreted as 'atf' with 'fa' (sequence), requiring both acts in immediate succession. This detailed linguistic analysis demonstrates the Hanafi method of interpreting particles based on context and legal consequences.

Key Terms
حتی (hatta): A particle that can mean ghayah (end/goal), sababiyya (causation/lam), or sequence (like fa) depending on context.
غایت (ghayah): The end or limit of an action; what comes after 'hatta' that terminates the action before it.
سبیت (sababiyya): Causality; when 'hatta' indicates cause or reason for the preceding action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the oath 'If I do not come to you until you feed me dinner,' if the swearer came but was not fed, is he a hanith (breaker of oath) according to the Hanafi analysis?
A) Yes, because he did not fulfill the condition.
B) No, because 'hatta' here indicates causation, and his coming fulfilled the oath.
C) Yes, because the oath requires feeding.
D) No, because the swearer must eat for the oath to be broken.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the meaning of 'hatta' in oaths is determined by the nature of the acts, leading to distinct legal outcomes for ghayah, sababiyya, and atf.

Meanings of 'Ba' and 'Ala' in Oaths
Hanafi classification of 'ba' for ilsāq and 'ala' for ilzām

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the primary meanings of 'ba' and 'ala' in oaths and apply the Hanafi rule to determine how an oath is fulfilled.

Core Idea
'Ba' attaches; 'ala' obliges and conditions, but in compensations 'ala' can attach.

The Hanafi school gives precise legal meanings to common Arabic prepositions when used in oaths and contracts. This lesson unpacks the rules for 'ba' and 'ala' as stated in the classical text. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly interpreting the scope and fulfillment of sworn statements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the preposition in the oath phrase.
Locate whether the oath uses 'ba' or 'ala' immediately after the verb of swearing or informing.
Example: 'akhbartani bi qudumi' uses 'ba'; 'ala alf' uses 'ala'.
2
Recall the primary meaning assigned by Hanafi usul.
'Ba' is for ilsāq (direct attachment). 'Ala' is for ilzām (obligation) and is also used for condition (shart).
This is a lexical rule: the meaning is not arbitrary but tied to established usul.
3
Apply the meaning to the oath to determine fulfillment.
For 'ba', the oath is fulfilled by the direct attachment of the matter (e.g., truthful news). For 'ala', the oath imposes a binding condition that must be satisfied.
4
Note the special use of 'ala' in pure compensations (mu'awadat mahdah).
In contracts like sales, 'ala' can be borrowed (musta'ar) to mean 'ba', because ilsāq (attachment) suits the binding nature (luzūm) of such transactions.
This shows flexibility in usul: metaphorical extension is allowed when the context demands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنْ ذَلِكَ حُرُوفُ الْجَرَ فَالْبَاءَ لِلْإِلْصَاقِ وَلِهَذَا قُلْنَا فِي قَوْلِهِ إِنْ أَخْبَرْتَنِيْ بِقُدُوْم فَلَانٍ أَنَّهُ يَقَعُ عَلَى الصِّدْقِ وَعَلَى لِلْألْزَامِ فِى قَوْلِهِ عَلَى اَلْفْ وَتَسْتَعْمَلُ لِلشَّرْطِ قَالَ الله تَعَالَى يُبَا يَعْنَكَ عَلَى أَنْ لَا يُشْرِكْنَ بِااللَّهِ شَيْئًا وَتُسْتَعَارُ بِمَعْنَى الْبَاءِ فِي الْمُعَاوَضَاتِ الْمَحْضَةِ لِاَنَّ الْإِلْصَاقَ يُنَاسِبُ اللُّزُوْمَ - ترجمہ: اور حروف معانی میں سے حروف جر ہیں، پس باء الصاق کے لئے ہے، اسی وجہ سے ہم نے کہا قائل کے قول ان اخبرتنى بقدوم فلان “ میں کہ یہ کلام سچی خبر پر واقع ہوگا۔ اور علی الزام کے لئے ہے قائل کے قول ” علی الف میں اور شرط کے لئے بھی استعمال کیا جاتا ہے، اللہ تعالیٰ نے ارشاد فرمایا يباي يبايعنك على ان لا يشركن با الله شيئا اور کلمہ علی مستعار لیا جاتا ہے باء کے معنی میں معاوضات محضہ میں، اس لئے کہ الصاق لزوم کے مناسب ہے۔
And among that are the letters of jar (prepositions). So 'ba' is for ilsāq (attachment), and for this reason we said in his statement 'If you inform me of the arrival of so-and-so' that it falls upon truthful news. And 'ala' is for ilzām (obligation) in his statement 'ala alf', and it is used for condition. Allah says: 'They pledge allegiance to you upon that they will not associate anything with Allah.' And 'ala' is borrowed in the meaning of 'ba' in pure compensations, because ilsāq is suitable for luzūm (binding).
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi usul rule regarding the prepositions 'ba' and 'ala' in legal contexts, particularly oaths. 'Ba' indicates ilsāq (direct attachment), so in an oath like 'If you inform me of the arrival of so-and-so', the oath is fulfilled by truthful news – the information directly attaches to the arrival. 'Ala' indicates ilzām (obligation/binding); when used in an oath like 'ala alif' (or similar), it imposes a binding condition. It is also used for condition, as in the Quranic verse about the pledge of allegiance (Surah al-Mumtahina, verse 12): '...upon that they will not associate anything with Allah.' Here 'ala' links the condition. In pure compensations (mu'awadat mahdah, e.g., sales), 'ala' is borrowed to mean 'ba', because ilsāq (direct attachment) is suitable for luzūm (binding, obligation). This shows the Hanafi method of interpreting particles according to their primary meanings but allowing metaphorical extensions when context demands.

Key Terms
باء (ba): Preposition indicating ilsāq (direct attachment).
علی (ala): Preposition indicating ilzām (obligation) or condition.
الصاق (ilsāq): Attachment or direct connection: the meaning of 'ba'.
الزام (ilzām): Obligation or binding: the meaning of 'ala'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary meaning of the preposition 'ba' in Hanafi usul?
A) Ilzām (obligation)
B) Sababiyya (causation)
C) Ilsāq (attachment)
D) Ghayah (end)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'ba' signals direct attachment (ilsāq) and 'ala' signals obligation (ilzām) and condition; in pure compensations, 'ala' can be borrowed to mean 'ba'.
